# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes)
**Task Type:** Security Analysis (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a security engineer auditing the Kubernetes API server's RBAC authorization subsystem. Your goal is to trace the complete authorization flow from when an API request arrives to when a permission decision (allow/deny) is made, mapping the attack surface and identifying security controls.

## Your Task

Analyze the Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow and write a comprehensive security analysis. Trace how API requests are authorized, identify entry points where untrusted input enters the authorization decision path, map the data flow through authorization plugins, and assess the security posture of the RBAC implementation.

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Required Sections

### Files Examined
- List each file you analyzed and its role in the RBAC authorization flow

### Entry Points
1. Identify where API requests enter the authorization subsystem
2. Identify where RBAC policy data (roles, bindings) enters the system
3. Note any places where untrusted input could influence authorization decisions

### Data Flow
Trace the authorization flow through these stages:
1. **Request arrival** — HTTP handler receives the request
2. **Authentication** — Request identity is established
3. **Authorization filter** — Request is routed to authorizer chain
4. **RBAC evaluation** — Role and binding resolution, permission check
5. **Decision** — Allow/deny outcome and audit logging

For each stage, name the specific file, function, and data structures involved.

### Dependency Chain
Provide an ordered list of files from request entry to authorization decision.

### Analysis
- What vulnerability classes could apply (auth bypass, privilege escalation, policy misconfiguration)?
- What existing mitigations are in place?
- What are the security boundaries between authorization plugins?
- How does the authorizer chain (RBAC, Node, Webhook) interact?

### Summary
Concise description of the RBAC authorization security posture and key findings.

## Constraints

- **Analysis only** — do NOT modify any source files
- Be specific — include file paths, function names, and type names
- Focus on the `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/` directories

## Summary of the Analysis

The document provides a detailed security audit of the Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem, covering:

### **Key Sections:**

1. **Files Examined** — 8 core files mapped to their role in the authorization pipeline, from HTTP filter invocation through rule resolution

2. **Entry Points** — Identified three critical entry points:
   - HTTP request handler (authorization filter)
   - RBAC policy data (roles/bindings from informers)
   - User identity (from authentication context)

3. **Data Flow** — Traced all 5 stages:
   - Request arrival and handler invocation
   - Authentication filter execution
   - RequestInfo extraction (URL/resource parsing)
   - Authorization attribute construction
   - Authorization decision and plugin chain evaluation

4. **Dependency Chain** — Ordered list of 8 core files from HTTP request to authorization decision, with cross-cutting dependencies on metrics and audit

5. **Security Analysis** — Comprehensive threat model covering:
   - Authentication bypass risks
   - Request intent misinterpretation
   - Policy misconfiguration leading to privilege escalation
   - Service account token compromise
   - Authorizer chain ordering vulnerabilities
   - Detailed mapping to CWE vulnerability classes

6. **Security Controls** — 5 detailed controls (RequestInfo validation, user context injection, rule evaluation, subject matching, role resolution) with bypass potential assessment

7. **Summary** — Strengths (separation of concerns, default-deny, stateless design) and weaknesses (misconfiguration risk, disabled authorization), plus 8 actionable security recommendations

24. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem implements a principled, defense-in-depth security model for API request authorization. The flow separates concerns across authentication (identity establishment), request parsing (intent extraction), and authorization decision (rule evaluation). RBAC operates within a pluggable authorizer chain that allows integration with alternative authorization mechanisms (Node, Webhook, ABAC). The implementation demonstrates strong security controls through stateless decision-making, immutable rule definitions, and clear separation of duties.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Authorization Infrastructure\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`** \u2014 HTTP filter intercepting requests and invoking authorizer chain; entry point for authorization decisions\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`** \u2014 Authorizer interface definitions and AttributesRecord (request metadata carrier)\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** \u2014 Authorizer chain composition enabling multiple authorizers with short-circuit allow/deny semantics\n\n### RBAC Authorization Implementation\n- **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 RBACAuthorizer implementation; core rule evaluation and allow/deny decision logic\n- **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 DefaultRuleResolver; role and binding resolution, subject matching, rule accumulation\n- **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer instantiation with informer-based role/binding listers\n\n### Request Processing Pipeline\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`** \u2014 RequestInfo extraction from HTTP request (verb, resource, namespace, name parsing)\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`** \u2014 User identity extraction from authentication result and context injection\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. HTTP Request Entry Point\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:53-98` (`WithAuthorization` function)\n\n**Entry Mechanism:**\n- HTTP handler intercepts incoming requests in the filter chain\n- Function: `withAuthorization(handler http.Handler, a authorizer.Authorizer, ...)`\n- Attaches HTTP handler wrapper that extracts attributes and invokes authorizer before calling next handler\n- **Untrusted Input:** Raw HTTP request including URL path, HTTP method, headers, request body\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Authorization filter operates on authenticated user identity (from context)\n- No direct authentication state available at this layer; depends on prior authentication filter execution\n- If authorization is disabled (`a == nil`), request passes through without authorization check (information disclosure risk)\n\n### 2. RBAC Policy Data Entry Points\n\n**Roles and Bindings Storage:**\n- **Role/Binding Listers:** `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:102-116`\n  - `RoleGetter.GetRole(ctx, namespace, name)` \u2014 Retrieves Role from informer cache\n  - `RoleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings(ctx, namespace)` \u2014 Lists all RoleBindings in namespace\n  - `ClusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole(ctx, name)` \u2014 Retrieves ClusterRole from cluster-wide cache\n  - `ClusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings(ctx)` \u2014 Lists all ClusterRoleBindings\n\n- **Data Source:** Kubernetes API objects (RBAC v1 API types) stored in etcd and cached in-memory via listers\n- **Untrusted Input:** All role and binding definitions can be modified by users with appropriate permissions\n- **Risk:** Misconfigured roles/bindings can grant excessive permissions; poisoned policies could lead to privilege escalation\n\n**Bootstrap Policy:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/`\n- Contains hardcoded system roles (system:admin, system:discovery, etc.)\n- Loaded at API server startup for default RBAC configuration\n- **Security Implication:** Defined in code, not user-modifiable during runtime\n\n### 3. User Identity Entry Point\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:100-151` (`GetAuthorizerAttributes` function, line 103-106)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- User identity extracted from request context: `request.UserFrom(ctx)`\n- Source: Result of authentication filter execution\n- Contains: User name, groups, UID, extra attributes\n\n**User Information Fields:**\n```\n- User.GetName() \u2014 Username (e.g., \"system:serviceaccount:default:default\")\n- User.GetGroups() \u2014 Group memberships (e.g., [\"system:authenticated\", \"system:serviceaccounts\"])\n- User.GetUID() \u2014 Unique identifier\n- User.GetExtra() \u2014 Additional attributes from authentication method\n```\n\n**Untrusted Aspects:**\n- Derived from HTTP headers (with authentication/front-proxy validation)\n- Service account tokens parsed and validated before reaching authorization\n- Group membership potentially spoofable if front-proxy authentication enabled without strict header validation\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Stage 1: Request Arrival and HTTP Handler Invocation\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:62-97`\n\n**Flow:**\n1. HTTP request arrives at server\n2. Authorization filter wrapper created by `WithAuthorization()` intercepts request\n3. Handler function invoked with (ResponseWriter, *http.Request)\n4. Request context contains prior results from:\n   - Authentication filter (User identity)\n   - RequestInfo filter (Resource information)\n\n**Data Structures:**\n- `http.Request` \u2014 Standard Go HTTP request with URL, method, headers\n- `context.Context` \u2014 Request context carrying:\n  - `request.UserFrom(ctx)` \u2192 `user.Info` interface\n  - `request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx)` \u2192 `request.RequestInfo` struct\n\n**Security Control:** Request has already passed authentication; user identity established and validated\n\n---\n\n### Stage 2: Authentication Filter Execution (Prior to Authorization)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go:46-110` (`WithAuthentication` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Authenticator invoked: `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` \u2192 `(resp *authenticator.Response, ok bool, err error)`\n2. Response contains authenticated user identity\n3. User info stored in request context: `request.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n4. Authorization header and front-proxy headers removed from request\n5. Request context passed to next filter (authorization)\n\n**User Info Construction Sources:**\n- **Client certificates:** Certificate subject parsed to user identity\n- **Bearer tokens:** Service account token validated, user.Info populated from token claims\n- **Request headers:** X-Remote-User, X-Remote-Group headers parsed (with front-proxy validation)\n- **OIDC tokens:** Token introspection, user claims extracted\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Authentication prevents unauthorized request progression\n- User identity guaranteed authentic at authorization filter entry\n- Risk: Compromised authenticator could inject false identities\n\n---\n\n### Stage 3: RequestInfo Extraction (Parallel to Auth)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go:28-41` (`WithRequestInfo` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. RequestInfoResolver parses HTTP request\n2. Extracts: verb, resource, namespace, name, API group, version, subresource, path\n3. For resource requests: `GET /apis/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod` \u2192\n   ```\n   ResourceRequest: true\n   Verb: \"get\"\n   APIGroup: \"\"\n   APIVersion: \"v1\"\n   Resource: \"pods\"\n   Namespace: \"default\"\n   Name: \"my-pod\"\n   Subresource: \"\"\n   ```\n4. For non-resource requests: `GET /healthz` \u2192\n   ```\n   ResourceRequest: false\n   Path: \"/healthz\"\n   Verb: \"get\"\n   ```\n\n**Data Structures:**\n```go\ntype RequestInfo struct {\n    IsResourceRequest bool\n    Path string\n    Verb string\n    APIGroup string\n    APIVersion string\n    Resource string\n    Subresource string\n    Namespace string\n    Name string\n    FieldSelector string\n    LabelSelector string\n}\n```\n\n**Security Considerations:**\n- **Untrusted Input:** URL path, query parameters parsed from user-controlled HTTP request\n- **Parsing Logic:** RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo() performs semantic parsing\n- **Risk:** Parsing errors could bypass authorization or misinterpret request intent\n- **Mitigation:** RequestInfo creation fails if parsing errors occur; error logged and InternalError returned (blocks request)\n\n---\n\n### Stage 4: Authorization Attribute Construction\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:100-151` (`GetAuthorizerAttributes` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Function constructs `AttributesRecord` from request context\n2. Combines user identity + request metadata\n3. Optionally parses label and field selectors (if feature gate enabled)\n\n**Attribute Record Construction:**\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{\n    User: <from context>,                    // authenticated user identity\n    ResourceRequest: requestInfo.IsResourceRequest,\n    Path: requestInfo.Path,\n    Verb: requestInfo.Verb,\n    APIGroup: requestInfo.APIGroup,\n    APIVersion: requestInfo.APIVersion,\n    Resource: requestInfo.Resource,\n    Subresource: requestInfo.Subresource,\n    Namespace: requestInfo.Namespace,\n    Name: requestInfo.Name,\n    FieldSelectorRequirements: <parsed>,     // optional, if AuthorizeWithSelectors enabled\n    LabelSelectorRequirements: <parsed>,     // optional, if AuthorizeWithSelectors enabled\n}\n```\n\n**Data Sources:**\n- User: From authentication result\n- Request metadata: From RequestInfo extraction\n- Selectors: From HTTP query parameters (untrusted, parsed with error handling)\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Attributes represent complete request context available to authorizer\n- If RequestInfo missing: InternalError returned, request blocked\n- Selector parsing errors caught and stored; authorization decision can account for parsing failures\n\n---\n\n### Stage 5: Authorization Decision and Plugin Chain\n\n#### 5A: Authorizer Chain Composition\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go:44-69` (`unionAuthzHandler.Authorize` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Union authorizer iterates over configured authorizers in order\n2. Each authorizer called with attributes\n3. Decision outcomes:\n   - `DecisionAllow` \u2014 Request permitted, short-circuit\n   - `DecisionDeny` \u2014 Request forbidden, short-circuit\n   - `DecisionNoOpinion` \u2014 Continue to next authorizer\n4. If all authorizers return NoOpinion: Aggregate decision is NoOpinion (effectively deny)\n5. Errors from each authorizer accumulated and returned\n\n**Chain Example (Typical Kubernetes):**\n```\n1. Node Authorizer     (kubelet-specific requests)\n   \u2193\n2. RBAC Authorizer     (role-based access control)\n   \u2193\n3. Webhook Authorizer  (external authorization)\n   \u2193\n4. Result: DecisionNoOpinion (deny)\n```\n\n**Security Properties:**\n- **Short-circuit Allow:** Any authorizer can permit request (fast path)\n- **No Short-circuit Deny:** Single deny doesn't stop evaluation (informational)\n- **Default Deny:** NoOpinion from all authorizers = deny\n- **Error Handling:** Errors accumulated and returned with decision\n\n**Risk:** Weak ordering could allow less-restrictive authorizer to permit request before stricter authorizer evaluation\n\n#### 5B: RBAC Evaluation\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:75-127` (`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n\n1. **Initialize visitor:** Create `authorizingVisitor` to track allowed status, reason, errors\n\n2. **Rule Resolution:** Invoke rule resolver\n   ```go\n   r.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(\n       ctx,\n       requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n       requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n       ruleCheckingVisitor.visit\n   )\n   ```\n\n3. **For each matching rule:** Visitor callback invoked\n   ```go\n   visit(source, rule, err) bool {\n       if rule != nil && RuleAllows(requestAttributes, rule) {\n           allowed = true\n           reason = fmt.Sprintf(\"RBAC: allowed by %s\", source.String())\n           return false  // short-circuit\n       }\n       if err != nil {\n           errors = append(errors, err)\n       }\n       return true  // continue\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Decision:** Return (DecisionAllow, reason, nil) if allowed, else (DecisionNoOpinion, reason, err)\n\n**Key Decision Function:** `RuleAllows(requestAttributes, rule)` at line 178-193\n\n---\n\n#### 5C: Rule Resolution and Subject Matching\n\n**File:** `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:179-237` (`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n\n1. **ClusterRoleBindings Query:**\n   ```go\n   clusterRoleBindings, err := r.clusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings(ctx)\n   ```\n   - Lists all ClusterRoleBindings from cluster (no namespace filtering)\n\n2. **Subject Matching:** For each binding, check if user applies to any subject\n   ```go\n   subjectIndex, applies := appliesTo(user, binding.Subjects, \"\")\n   ```\n\n3. **Role Reference Resolution:** If user matches, fetch referenced role/clusterrole\n   ```go\n   rules, err := r.GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, binding.RoleRef, \"\")\n   ```\n\n4. **Role Lookup:** `GetRoleReferenceRules()` at line 240-259\n   ```go\n   switch roleRef.Kind {\n       case \"Role\":\n           role, err := r.roleGetter.GetRole(ctx, namespace, name)\n           return role.Rules, err\n       case \"ClusterRole\":\n           clusterRole, err := r.clusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole(ctx, name)\n           return clusterRole.Rules, err\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Subject Matching Logic:** `appliesToUser()` at line 281-300\n   ```\n   - UserKind: user.GetName() == subject.Name\n   - GroupKind: user in user.GetGroups()\n   - ServiceAccountKind:\n       * serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(namespace, name, user.GetName())\n       * Default to request namespace if subject.Namespace empty\n   ```\n\n6. **Namespace-scoped RoleBindings:** (if namespace provided)\n   ```go\n   if len(namespace) > 0 {\n       roleBindings, err := r.roleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings(ctx, namespace)\n       // Repeat subject matching and rule resolution\n   }\n   ```\n\n**Data Structures:**\n```go\n// RoleBinding references a role and subjects\ntype RoleBinding struct {\n    Name: \"my-binding\"\n    Namespace: \"default\"\n    Subjects: [{Kind: \"User\", Name: \"alice\"}]\n    RoleRef: {Kind: \"Role\", Name: \"editor\"}\n}\n\n// Role contains policy rules\ntype Role struct {\n    Name: \"editor\"\n    Rules: [\n        {Verbs: [\"get\", \"list\"], Resources: [\"pods\"], APIGroups: [\"\"]}\n    ]\n}\n\n// PolicyRule grants permissions\ntype PolicyRule struct {\n    Verbs: [\"get\", \"list\"]\n    APIGroups: [\"\"]\n    Resources: [\"pods\"]\n    ResourceNames: []  // specific instances\n    NonResourceURLs: [] // non-API paths\n}\n```\n\n**Security Consideration:** Rule matching is **purely additive** \u2014 if ANY rule allows, request is allowed. No deny rules in RBAC.\n\n#### 5D: Rule Matching\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:178-193` (`RuleAllows` function)\n\n**Resource Request Matching:**\n```go\nif requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n    combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource  // e.g., \"pods/logs\"\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n           APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n           ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n           ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n}\n```\n\n**Non-Resource Request Matching:**\n```go\nreturn VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n       NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n```\n\n**Matching Semantics:**\n- Verb: Exact match (including wildcards in rules)\n- APIGroup: Match against `rule.APIGroups` or \"*\" wildcard\n- Resource: Match against `rule.Resources` or \"*\" wildcard\n- ResourceName: Match against `rule.ResourceNames` or \"\" (all) or specific names\n- Path: Match against `rule.NonResourceURLs` (glob patterns)\n\n**Deny Decisions:** If no rules match, visitor never signals allow \u2192 (DecisionNoOpinion, error)\n\n---\n\n### Summary: Complete Authorization Path\n\n```\nHTTP Request Arrives\n    \u2193\nAuthentication Filter\n    \u2192 Extracts/validates user identity\n    \u2193\nRequestInfo Filter\n    \u2192 Parses URL, extracts resource metadata\n    \u2193\nAuthorization Filter (WithAuthorization)\n    \u2192 Constructs AttributesRecord\n    \u2193\nUnion Authorizer Chain\n    \u2193\nRBAC Authorizer.Authorize()\n    \u2193\nDefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()\n    \u2192 ListClusterRoleBindings()\n    \u2192 For each: appliesTo(user, subjects) + GetRoleReferenceRules(roleRef)\n    \u2192 Accumulate matching rules\n    \u2192 ListRoleBindings(namespace)\n    \u2192 Repeat for namespace-scoped bindings\n    \u2193\nFor each rule: RuleAllows(attributes, rule)\n    \u2193\nDecision: DecisionAllow | DecisionNoOpinion\n    \u2193\nBack to Filter: Allow request or respond 403 Forbidden\n```\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from HTTP request arrival to authorization decision:\n\n1. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`** \u2014 User identity extraction\n2. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`** \u2014 Request metadata parsing\n3. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`** \u2014 Attribute construction + authorizer invocation entry point\n4. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`** \u2014 Authorizer interface definition\n5. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** \u2014 Authorizer chain orchestration\n6. **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer core logic\n7. **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 Rule resolver and subject matching\n8. **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer instantiation and informer wiring\n\n**Cross-cutting Dependencies:**\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/metrics`** \u2014 Decision metrics recording\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit`** \u2014 Audit annotation injection\n- **`k8s.io/client-go/listers`** \u2014 RBAC informer caches (Roles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoles, ClusterRoleBindings)\n\n---\n\n## Security Analysis\n\n### 1. Threat Model: Attack Surface\n\n#### A. Authentication Bypass\n- **Vector:** Attacker establishes false user identity to authorization system\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Authentication filter validates credentials (certificates, tokens, headers) before context injection\n  - Authorization operates on authentication result; cannot enforce stronger auth controls\n  - User identity extracted via `request.UserFrom(ctx)` \u2014 immutable once in context\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Depends entirely on authentication subsystem strength\n\n#### B. Request Intent Misinterpretation\n- **Vector:** Attacker crafts ambiguous URL/request to be parsed differently by authorization vs. handler\n- **Attack Example:** Request `/apis/v1/pods` parsed as resource=\"pods\", handler interprets as resource=\"apiserver\"\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - RequestInfo parser enforces strict RFC-compliant URL parsing\n  - Single RequestInfo instance shared between authorization and handler\n  - Authorization decision based on parsed resource, not raw URL\n- **Risk Level:** LOW \u2014 Shared RequestInfo prevents divergence\n\n#### C. Policy Misconfiguration Leading to Privilege Escalation\n- **Vector:** RBAC administrator creates overly permissive roles (e.g., `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"]`)\n- **Example:** Wildcard ClusterRole binding to all users\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Built-in validation for Role/RoleBinding creation (webhook admission)\n  - RBAC system does not enforce policy semantic validation \u2014 relies on operator discipline\n  - **Audit trail:** Audit log records role/binding changes\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH \u2014 No semantic enforcement; depends on policy review and audit\n\n#### D. Service Account Token Compromise\n- **Vector:** Attacker obtains service account token (from pod, deployment, etc.)\n- **Effect:** Authorizer treats attacker as service account; grants permissions bound to that identity\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Token stored in namespaced Secret; RBAC governs read access\n  - Token audience-validated during authentication\n  - Lifespan/expiration enforced\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH \u2014 If token obtained, permissions automatically granted; no additional authorization required\n\n#### E. Man-in-the-Middle on Authorizer-Informer Communication\n- **Vector:** Attacker intercepts informer updates (Role/Binding changes from etcd)\n- **Effect:** Authorization decisions based on stale or poisoned policy data\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Listers use in-memory cache from informers\n  - Informers validate etcd connection and watch stream integrity\n  - Authorization falls back to error handling if informer fails\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Requires network-level access; audit trail captures policy changes\n\n#### F. Short-Circuit Logic Abuse in Authorizer Chain\n- **Vector:** Attacker exploits authorizer ordering (e.g., permissive Node authorizer checked first)\n- **Attack Example:** Kubelet-specific request matches Node authorizer before RBAC can deny\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Authorizer chain order is configuration-dependent\n  - Short-circuit only occurs on Allow/Deny; NoOpinion continues\n  - Each authorizer independent; no state leakage\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Depends on chain configuration; documented in authorizer docs\n\n### 2. Vulnerability Classes and Mitigations\n\n#### Authorization Bypass (CWE-285)\n- **Mechanism:** Bypass of policy evaluation through:\n  - Parsing ambiguity (partially mitigated by shared RequestInfo)\n  - Empty authorizer list (code-level check: \"at least one authorization mode\")\n  - Disabled authorization (authorization filter logs warning; bypasses authorization)\n- **Mitigation Strength:** STRONG for parsing; WEAK for disabled authorization\n- **Recommendation:** Enforce authorization mode via startup validation\n\n#### Privilege Escalation (CWE-269)\n- **Mechanism:** User granted excessive permissions through:\n  - Overly permissive roles (no automated validation)\n  - Wildcard selectors in policy rules\n  - Service account privilege inheritance\n- **Mitigation Strength:** WEAK \u2014 Relies on policy discipline\n- **Recommendation:** Implement policy scanning/validation tooling; enforce least-privilege admissions webhooks\n\n#### Information Disclosure (CWE-200)\n- **Mechanism:** Authorization disabled; rules exposed via introspection\n- **Mitigation Strength:** WEAK if authorization disabled\n- **Recommendation:** Mandatory authorization configuration; audit tool to detect disabled authorization\n\n#### Authentication Coercion (CWE-287)\n- **Vector:** Attacker impersonates user by:\n  - Forging request headers (if using header-based auth without mTLS)\n  - Reusing stolen tokens\n- **Mitigation:** Depends on authentication method (certificate validation, token lifecycle)\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH if front-proxy auth without strict validation\n\n### 3. Data Flow Security Properties\n\n#### Immutability of Authorization Input\n- **User Identity:** Once extracted by authentication filter and stored in context, immutable\n- **Request Metadata:** RequestInfo constructed once, shared throughout request lifecycle\n- **Attributes:** AttributesRecord is value-type (passed by copy in Go)\n- **Security Property:** Authorization decisions based on stable, non-modifiable input\n\n#### Stateless Authorization\n- **RBACAuthorizer:** Stateless; no session/cache between requests\n- **DefaultRuleResolver:** Queries fresh authorizer-cached data per request\n- **Security Property:** No cross-request state leakage; replay protection inherent\n\n#### Error Handling\n- **Rule Resolution Errors:** Caught during traversal; cause return of (DecisionNoOpinion, error)\n- **Partial Failures:** If one role lookup fails, other rules still evaluated (partial policy evaluation)\n- **RequestInfo Parse Errors:** InternalError returned; request blocked\n- **Security Property:** Failures generally deny access; graceful degradation possible\n\n### 4. Security Boundaries\n\n#### Authorization Filter Boundary\n- **Input:** HTTP request + context (user, requestInfo)\n- **Output:** Allow/Deny decision\n- **Cross-boundary Trust:** Assumes authentication filter trustworthiness\n\n#### Authorizer Chain Boundary\n- **Union Authorizer:** Orchestrates multiple authorizers\n- **Assumption:** Individual authorizers are trustworthy; no authorization checks between them\n- **Risk:** Single compromised authorizer (e.g., malicious Node authorizer) can permit requests\n\n#### RBAC-to-Storage Boundary\n- **Data Source:** Listers (informer caches) for roles/bindings\n- **Assumption:** Informer cache is synchronized with etcd\n- **Risk:** Stale cache could apply outdated policies (low probability due to watch semantics)\n\n#### User Identity Boundary\n- **Source:** Authentication result (user.Info)\n- **Assumption:** User identity is authentic and complete\n- **Risk:** Authentication compromise propagates to authorization (HIGH severity, out-of-scope for auth)\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Security Controls\n\n### Control 1: RequestInfo Validation\n- **Location:** `authorization.go:100-111`, `requestinfo.go:28-41`\n- **Function:** Ensures request intent is correctly parsed before authorization\n- **Enforcement:** Missing RequestInfo \u2192 InternalError (blocks request)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 RequestInfo construction fails loudly\n\n### Control 2: User Context Injection\n- **Location:** `authentication.go:46-110`\n- **Function:** Authenticates user and injects identity into context\n- **Enforcement:** No authentication \u2192 failed.ServeHTTP (denies request)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 User identity required for authorization\n\n### Control 3: Rule Evaluation\n- **Location:** `rbac.go:75-127`, `rule.go:179-237`\n- **Function:** Enumerates all applicable rules and checks for permission match\n- **Enforcement:** No matching rule \u2192 DecisionNoOpinion (effectively deny)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Complete rule traversal, no early termination unless rule matches\n\n### Control 4: Subject Matching\n- **Location:** `rule.go:263-300` (`appliesTo`, `appliesToUser`)\n- **Function:** Verifies user matches binding subjects (by name, group, service account)\n- **Enforcement:** appliesToUser() implements strict comparison logic\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Direct string/group comparison; no glob patterns in subject names\n\n### Control 5: Role Reference Resolution\n- **Location:** `rule.go:240-259` (`GetRoleReferenceRules`)\n- **Function:** Validates role reference kind (Role vs. ClusterRole) and looks up rules\n- **Enforcement:** Unknown role reference kind \u2192 error\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Explicit kind switch, no implicit resolution\n\n---\n\n## Audit and Observability\n\n### Audit Trail\n- **Location:** `authorization.go:80-96`\n- **Information Recorded:**\n  - Decision (allow/forbid)\n  - Reason (e.g., \"RBAC: allowed by ClusterRoleBinding xyz\")\n  - Authorization duration\n- **Audit Events:** Integration with `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit` for request-level logging\n\n### Logging\n- **Decision Denials:** Logged at V=4 level (debug)\n- **Detailed Denials:** Logged at V=5 level (very verbose), showing all attempted rules\n- **Example:** `\"RBAC: no rules authorize user %q with groups %q to %s %s\"`\n\n### Metrics\n- **Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/metrics.go`\n- **Metrics:** Decision counts, latency, error rates by decision type\n\n---\n\n## Known Limitations and Mitigations\n\n| Limitation | Implication | Mitigation |\n|---|---|---|\n| **No Deny Rules** | RBAC is purely additive; cannot explicitly deny | Design policies carefully; use negative space (don't grant permission) |\n| **No Conditional Rules** | Rules cannot depend on runtime context (e.g., time-based) | Use external webhook authorizer for conditional logic |\n| **No Resource Quota/Enforcement** | Authorization doesn't limit resource consumption | Use ResourceQuota and admission webhooks |\n| **Cluster-wide Rules Evaluated for Namespace Requests** | Namespace-scoped requests checked against ClusterRoleBindings | Expected behavior; allows cross-namespace role references |\n| **Service Account Privilege Inheritance** | Service account inherits all bindings in its namespace | Principle of least privilege; separate service accounts per function |\n| **Deprecated Auth Methods** | Legacy ABAC, static files deprecated | Migrate to RBAC or webhook authorization |\n\n---\n\n## Summary: RBAC Authorization Security Posture\n\n### Strengths\n1. **Clear Separation of Concerns:** Authentication (identity) \u2192 Authorization (policy enforcement) \u2192 Admission (resource semantic validation)\n2. **Pluggable Architecture:** Multiple authorizers can coexist; flexible integration with external systems\n3. **Stateless Design:** No cross-request state; immunity to replay/timing attacks\n4. **Default-Deny Model:** Authorizer chain defaults to NoOpinion (deny) if no rule matches\n5. **Audit Integration:** Full request lifecycle logged; decisions and denials traceable\n6. **Informer-based Caching:** Efficient in-memory policy evaluation without etcd query per request\n7. **Short-circuit Semantics:** Both Allow and Deny decisions halt further evaluation; no policy contradiction\n\n### Weaknesses\n1. **Policy Misconfiguration Risk:** No built-in validation of role semantics; overly permissive roles possible\n2. **Service Account Token Compromise:** Once token obtained, full permissions granted without additional checks\n3. **Authorizer Chain Ordering:** Permissive authorizers checked first could permit requests prematurely\n4. **Disabled Authorization:** If authorization mode disabled, all requests allowed (warning only)\n5. **No Time-based or Contextual Rules:** RBAC is static; cannot encode temporal constraints or conditional logic\n\n### Key Security Recommendations\n1. **Enforce Authorization Mode:** Mandate authorization at API server startup (not optional)\n2. **Restrict Service Account Token Scope:** Bind tokens to specific audiences; minimize blast radius if compromised\n3. **Audit Role/Binding Changes:** Monitor for policy modifications; alert on suspicious changes\n4. **Implement Policy Validation:** Scanning tool to detect overly permissive roles before deployment\n5. **Least-Privilege Service Accounts:** Create minimal service accounts for workloads; avoid shared accounts\n6. **Review Authorizer Chain:** Verify ordering; ensure more restrictive authorizers evaluated before permissive ones\n7. **Secure Informer Communication:** Validate informer cache freshness; monitor for sync failures\n8. **Monitor Denial Patterns:** Alert on repeated authorization denials for high-privilege operations\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization system implements a well-architected, defense-in-depth security model. Request authorization is decoupled from authentication and admission, enabling flexible policy enforcement. The stateless, plugin-based design provides strong fundamentals for secure access control. However, the security posture depends critically on proper policy configuration, secure secret management (for service account tokens), and comprehensive audit monitoring. Organizations deploying Kubernetes must combine RBAC with operational discipline (least-privilege design, policy review, incident response) to achieve robust authorization security.\n",

  "content": "# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem implements a principled, defense-in-depth security model for API request authorization. The flow separates concerns across authentication (identity establishment), request parsing (intent extraction), and authorization decision (rule evaluation). RBAC operates within a pluggable authorizer chain that allows integration with alternative authorization mechanisms (Node, Webhook, ABAC). The implementation demonstrates strong security controls through stateless decision-making, immutable rule definitions, and clear separation of duties.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Authorization Infrastructure\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`** \u2014 HTTP filter intercepting requests and invoking authorizer chain; entry point for authorization decisions\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`** \u2014 Authorizer interface definitions and AttributesRecord (request metadata carrier)\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** \u2014 Authorizer chain composition enabling multiple authorizers with short-circuit allow/deny semantics\n\n### RBAC Authorization Implementation\n- **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 RBACAuthorizer implementation; core rule evaluation and allow/deny decision logic\n- **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 DefaultRuleResolver; role and binding resolution, subject matching, rule accumulation\n- **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer instantiation with informer-based role/binding listers\n\n### Request Processing Pipeline\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`** \u2014 RequestInfo extraction from HTTP request (verb, resource, namespace, name parsing)\n- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`** \u2014 User identity extraction from authentication result and context injection\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. HTTP Request Entry Point\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:53-98` (`WithAuthorization` function)\n\n**Entry Mechanism:**\n- HTTP handler intercepts incoming requests in the filter chain\n- Function: `withAuthorization(handler http.Handler, a authorizer.Authorizer, ...)`\n- Attaches HTTP handler wrapper that extracts attributes and invokes authorizer before calling next handler\n- **Untrusted Input:** Raw HTTP request including URL path, HTTP method, headers, request body\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Authorization filter operates on authenticated user identity (from context)\n- No direct authentication state available at this layer; depends on prior authentication filter execution\n- If authorization is disabled (`a == nil`), request passes through without authorization check (information disclosure risk)\n\n### 2. RBAC Policy Data Entry Points\n\n**Roles and Bindings Storage:**\n- **Role/Binding Listers:** `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:102-116`\n  - `RoleGetter.GetRole(ctx, namespace, name)` \u2014 Retrieves Role from informer cache\n  - `RoleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings(ctx, namespace)` \u2014 Lists all RoleBindings in namespace\n  - `ClusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole(ctx, name)` \u2014 Retrieves ClusterRole from cluster-wide cache\n  - `ClusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings(ctx)` \u2014 Lists all ClusterRoleBindings\n\n- **Data Source:** Kubernetes API objects (RBAC v1 API types) stored in etcd and cached in-memory via listers\n- **Untrusted Input:** All role and binding definitions can be modified by users with appropriate permissions\n- **Risk:** Misconfigured roles/bindings can grant excessive permissions; poisoned policies could lead to privilege escalation\n\n**Bootstrap Policy:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/`\n- Contains hardcoded system roles (system:admin, system:discovery, etc.)\n- Loaded at API server startup for default RBAC configuration\n- **Security Implication:** Defined in code, not user-modifiable during runtime\n\n### 3. User Identity Entry Point\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:100-151` (`GetAuthorizerAttributes` function, line 103-106)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- User identity extracted from request context: `request.UserFrom(ctx)`\n- Source: Result of authentication filter execution\n- Contains: User name, groups, UID, extra attributes\n\n**User Information Fields:**\n```\n- User.GetName() \u2014 Username (e.g., \"system:serviceaccount:default:default\")\n- User.GetGroups() \u2014 Group memberships (e.g., [\"system:authenticated\", \"system:serviceaccounts\"])\n- User.GetUID() \u2014 Unique identifier\n- User.GetExtra() \u2014 Additional attributes from authentication method\n```\n\n**Untrusted Aspects:**\n- Derived from HTTP headers (with authentication/front-proxy validation)\n- Service account tokens parsed and validated before reaching authorization\n- Group membership potentially spoofable if front-proxy authentication enabled without strict header validation\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Stage 1: Request Arrival and HTTP Handler Invocation\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:62-97`\n\n**Flow:**\n1. HTTP request arrives at server\n2. Authorization filter wrapper created by `WithAuthorization()` intercepts request\n3. Handler function invoked with (ResponseWriter, *http.Request)\n4. Request context contains prior results from:\n   - Authentication filter (User identity)\n   - RequestInfo filter (Resource information)\n\n**Data Structures:**\n- `http.Request` \u2014 Standard Go HTTP request with URL, method, headers\n- `context.Context` \u2014 Request context carrying:\n  - `request.UserFrom(ctx)` \u2192 `user.Info` interface\n  - `request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx)` \u2192 `request.RequestInfo` struct\n\n**Security Control:** Request has already passed authentication; user identity established and validated\n\n---\n\n### Stage 2: Authentication Filter Execution (Prior to Authorization)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go:46-110` (`WithAuthentication` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Authenticator invoked: `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` \u2192 `(resp *authenticator.Response, ok bool, err error)`\n2. Response contains authenticated user identity\n3. User info stored in request context: `request.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n4. Authorization header and front-proxy headers removed from request\n5. Request context passed to next filter (authorization)\n\n**User Info Construction Sources:**\n- **Client certificates:** Certificate subject parsed to user identity\n- **Bearer tokens:** Service account token validated, user.Info populated from token claims\n- **Request headers:** X-Remote-User, X-Remote-Group headers parsed (with front-proxy validation)\n- **OIDC tokens:** Token introspection, user claims extracted\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Authentication prevents unauthorized request progression\n- User identity guaranteed authentic at authorization filter entry\n- Risk: Compromised authenticator could inject false identities\n\n---\n\n### Stage 3: RequestInfo Extraction (Parallel to Auth)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go:28-41` (`WithRequestInfo` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. RequestInfoResolver parses HTTP request\n2. Extracts: verb, resource, namespace, name, API group, version, subresource, path\n3. For resource requests: `GET /apis/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod` \u2192\n   ```\n   ResourceRequest: true\n   Verb: \"get\"\n   APIGroup: \"\"\n   APIVersion: \"v1\"\n   Resource: \"pods\"\n   Namespace: \"default\"\n   Name: \"my-pod\"\n   Subresource: \"\"\n   ```\n4. For non-resource requests: `GET /healthz` \u2192\n   ```\n   ResourceRequest: false\n   Path: \"/healthz\"\n   Verb: \"get\"\n   ```\n\n**Data Structures:**\n```go\ntype RequestInfo struct {\n    IsResourceRequest bool\n    Path string\n    Verb string\n    APIGroup string\n    APIVersion string\n    Resource string\n    Subresource string\n    Namespace string\n    Name string\n    FieldSelector string\n    LabelSelector string\n}\n```\n\n**Security Considerations:**\n- **Untrusted Input:** URL path, query parameters parsed from user-controlled HTTP request\n- **Parsing Logic:** RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo() performs semantic parsing\n- **Risk:** Parsing errors could bypass authorization or misinterpret request intent\n- **Mitigation:** RequestInfo creation fails if parsing errors occur; error logged and InternalError returned (blocks request)\n\n---\n\n### Stage 4: Authorization Attribute Construction\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:100-151` (`GetAuthorizerAttributes` function)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Function constructs `AttributesRecord` from request context\n2. Combines user identity + request metadata\n3. Optionally parses label and field selectors (if feature gate enabled)\n\n**Attribute Record Construction:**\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{\n    User: <from context>,                    // authenticated user identity\n    ResourceRequest: requestInfo.IsResourceRequest,\n    Path: requestInfo.Path,\n    Verb: requestInfo.Verb,\n    APIGroup: requestInfo.APIGroup,\n    APIVersion: requestInfo.APIVersion,\n    Resource: requestInfo.Resource,\n    Subresource: requestInfo.Subresource,\n    Namespace: requestInfo.Namespace,\n    Name: requestInfo.Name,\n    FieldSelectorRequirements: <parsed>,     // optional, if AuthorizeWithSelectors enabled\n    LabelSelectorRequirements: <parsed>,     // optional, if AuthorizeWithSelectors enabled\n}\n```\n\n**Data Sources:**\n- User: From authentication result\n- Request metadata: From RequestInfo extraction\n- Selectors: From HTTP query parameters (untrusted, parsed with error handling)\n\n**Security Boundary:**\n- Attributes represent complete request context available to authorizer\n- If RequestInfo missing: InternalError returned, request blocked\n- Selector parsing errors caught and stored; authorization decision can account for parsing failures\n\n---\n\n### Stage 5: Authorization Decision and Plugin Chain\n\n#### 5A: Authorizer Chain Composition\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go:44-69` (`unionAuthzHandler.Authorize` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Union authorizer iterates over configured authorizers in order\n2. Each authorizer called with attributes\n3. Decision outcomes:\n   - `DecisionAllow` \u2014 Request permitted, short-circuit\n   - `DecisionDeny` \u2014 Request forbidden, short-circuit\n   - `DecisionNoOpinion` \u2014 Continue to next authorizer\n4. If all authorizers return NoOpinion: Aggregate decision is NoOpinion (effectively deny)\n5. Errors from each authorizer accumulated and returned\n\n**Chain Example (Typical Kubernetes):**\n```\n1. Node Authorizer     (kubelet-specific requests)\n   \u2193\n2. RBAC Authorizer     (role-based access control)\n   \u2193\n3. Webhook Authorizer  (external authorization)\n   \u2193\n4. Result: DecisionNoOpinion (deny)\n```\n\n**Security Properties:**\n- **Short-circuit Allow:** Any authorizer can permit request (fast path)\n- **No Short-circuit Deny:** Single deny doesn't stop evaluation (informational)\n- **Default Deny:** NoOpinion from all authorizers = deny\n- **Error Handling:** Errors accumulated and returned with decision\n\n**Risk:** Weak ordering could allow less-restrictive authorizer to permit request before stricter authorizer evaluation\n\n#### 5B: RBAC Evaluation\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:75-127` (`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n\n1. **Initialize visitor:** Create `authorizingVisitor` to track allowed status, reason, errors\n\n2. **Rule Resolution:** Invoke rule resolver\n   ```go\n   r.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(\n       ctx,\n       requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n       requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n       ruleCheckingVisitor.visit\n   )\n   ```\n\n3. **For each matching rule:** Visitor callback invoked\n   ```go\n   visit(source, rule, err) bool {\n       if rule != nil && RuleAllows(requestAttributes, rule) {\n           allowed = true\n           reason = fmt.Sprintf(\"RBAC: allowed by %s\", source.String())\n           return false  // short-circuit\n       }\n       if err != nil {\n           errors = append(errors, err)\n       }\n       return true  // continue\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Decision:** Return (DecisionAllow, reason, nil) if allowed, else (DecisionNoOpinion, reason, err)\n\n**Key Decision Function:** `RuleAllows(requestAttributes, rule)` at line 178-193\n\n---\n\n#### 5C: Rule Resolution and Subject Matching\n\n**File:** `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:179-237` (`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` method)\n\n**Flow:**\n\n1. **ClusterRoleBindings Query:**\n   ```go\n   clusterRoleBindings, err := r.clusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings(ctx)\n   ```\n   - Lists all ClusterRoleBindings from cluster (no namespace filtering)\n\n2. **Subject Matching:** For each binding, check if user applies to any subject\n   ```go\n   subjectIndex, applies := appliesTo(user, binding.Subjects, \"\")\n   ```\n\n3. **Role Reference Resolution:** If user matches, fetch referenced role/clusterrole\n   ```go\n   rules, err := r.GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, binding.RoleRef, \"\")\n   ```\n\n4. **Role Lookup:** `GetRoleReferenceRules()` at line 240-259\n   ```go\n   switch roleRef.Kind {\n       case \"Role\":\n           role, err := r.roleGetter.GetRole(ctx, namespace, name)\n           return role.Rules, err\n       case \"ClusterRole\":\n           clusterRole, err := r.clusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole(ctx, name)\n           return clusterRole.Rules, err\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Subject Matching Logic:** `appliesToUser()` at line 281-300\n   ```\n   - UserKind: user.GetName() == subject.Name\n   - GroupKind: user in user.GetGroups()\n   - ServiceAccountKind:\n       * serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(namespace, name, user.GetName())\n       * Default to request namespace if subject.Namespace empty\n   ```\n\n6. **Namespace-scoped RoleBindings:** (if namespace provided)\n   ```go\n   if len(namespace) > 0 {\n       roleBindings, err := r.roleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings(ctx, namespace)\n       // Repeat subject matching and rule resolution\n   }\n   ```\n\n**Data Structures:**\n```go\n// RoleBinding references a role and subjects\ntype RoleBinding struct {\n    Name: \"my-binding\"\n    Namespace: \"default\"\n    Subjects: [{Kind: \"User\", Name: \"alice\"}]\n    RoleRef: {Kind: \"Role\", Name: \"editor\"}\n}\n\n// Role contains policy rules\ntype Role struct {\n    Name: \"editor\"\n    Rules: [\n        {Verbs: [\"get\", \"list\"], Resources: [\"pods\"], APIGroups: [\"\"]}\n    ]\n}\n\n// PolicyRule grants permissions\ntype PolicyRule struct {\n    Verbs: [\"get\", \"list\"]\n    APIGroups: [\"\"]\n    Resources: [\"pods\"]\n    ResourceNames: []  // specific instances\n    NonResourceURLs: [] // non-API paths\n}\n```\n\n**Security Consideration:** Rule matching is **purely additive** \u2014 if ANY rule allows, request is allowed. No deny rules in RBAC.\n\n#### 5D: Rule Matching\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:178-193` (`RuleAllows` function)\n\n**Resource Request Matching:**\n```go\nif requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n    combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource  // e.g., \"pods/logs\"\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n           APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n           ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n           ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n}\n```\n\n**Non-Resource Request Matching:**\n```go\nreturn VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n       NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n```\n\n**Matching Semantics:**\n- Verb: Exact match (including wildcards in rules)\n- APIGroup: Match against `rule.APIGroups` or \"*\" wildcard\n- Resource: Match against `rule.Resources` or \"*\" wildcard\n- ResourceName: Match against `rule.ResourceNames` or \"\" (all) or specific names\n- Path: Match against `rule.NonResourceURLs` (glob patterns)\n\n**Deny Decisions:** If no rules match, visitor never signals allow \u2192 (DecisionNoOpinion, error)\n\n---\n\n### Summary: Complete Authorization Path\n\n```\nHTTP Request Arrives\n    \u2193\nAuthentication Filter\n    \u2192 Extracts/validates user identity\n    \u2193\nRequestInfo Filter\n    \u2192 Parses URL, extracts resource metadata\n    \u2193\nAuthorization Filter (WithAuthorization)\n    \u2192 Constructs AttributesRecord\n    \u2193\nUnion Authorizer Chain\n    \u2193\nRBAC Authorizer.Authorize()\n    \u2193\nDefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()\n    \u2192 ListClusterRoleBindings()\n    \u2192 For each: appliesTo(user, subjects) + GetRoleReferenceRules(roleRef)\n    \u2192 Accumulate matching rules\n    \u2192 ListRoleBindings(namespace)\n    \u2192 Repeat for namespace-scoped bindings\n    \u2193\nFor each rule: RuleAllows(attributes, rule)\n    \u2193\nDecision: DecisionAllow | DecisionNoOpinion\n    \u2193\nBack to Filter: Allow request or respond 403 Forbidden\n```\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from HTTP request arrival to authorization decision:\n\n1. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`** \u2014 User identity extraction\n2. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`** \u2014 Request metadata parsing\n3. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`** \u2014 Attribute construction + authorizer invocation entry point\n4. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`** \u2014 Authorizer interface definition\n5. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** \u2014 Authorizer chain orchestration\n6. **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer core logic\n7. **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 Rule resolver and subject matching\n8. **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`** \u2014 RBAC authorizer instantiation and informer wiring\n\n**Cross-cutting Dependencies:**\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/metrics`** \u2014 Decision metrics recording\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit`** \u2014 Audit annotation injection\n- **`k8s.io/client-go/listers`** \u2014 RBAC informer caches (Roles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoles, ClusterRoleBindings)\n\n---\n\n## Security Analysis\n\n### 1. Threat Model: Attack Surface\n\n#### A. Authentication Bypass\n- **Vector:** Attacker establishes false user identity to authorization system\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Authentication filter validates credentials (certificates, tokens, headers) before context injection\n  - Authorization operates on authentication result; cannot enforce stronger auth controls\n  - User identity extracted via `request.UserFrom(ctx)` \u2014 immutable once in context\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Depends entirely on authentication subsystem strength\n\n#### B. Request Intent Misinterpretation\n- **Vector:** Attacker crafts ambiguous URL/request to be parsed differently by authorization vs. handler\n- **Attack Example:** Request `/apis/v1/pods` parsed as resource=\"pods\", handler interprets as resource=\"apiserver\"\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - RequestInfo parser enforces strict RFC-compliant URL parsing\n  - Single RequestInfo instance shared between authorization and handler\n  - Authorization decision based on parsed resource, not raw URL\n- **Risk Level:** LOW \u2014 Shared RequestInfo prevents divergence\n\n#### C. Policy Misconfiguration Leading to Privilege Escalation\n- **Vector:** RBAC administrator creates overly permissive roles (e.g., `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"]`)\n- **Example:** Wildcard ClusterRole binding to all users\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Built-in validation for Role/RoleBinding creation (webhook admission)\n  - RBAC system does not enforce policy semantic validation \u2014 relies on operator discipline\n  - **Audit trail:** Audit log records role/binding changes\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH \u2014 No semantic enforcement; depends on policy review and audit\n\n#### D. Service Account Token Compromise\n- **Vector:** Attacker obtains service account token (from pod, deployment, etc.)\n- **Effect:** Authorizer treats attacker as service account; grants permissions bound to that identity\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Token stored in namespaced Secret; RBAC governs read access\n  - Token audience-validated during authentication\n  - Lifespan/expiration enforced\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH \u2014 If token obtained, permissions automatically granted; no additional authorization required\n\n#### E. Man-in-the-Middle on Authorizer-Informer Communication\n- **Vector:** Attacker intercepts informer updates (Role/Binding changes from etcd)\n- **Effect:** Authorization decisions based on stale or poisoned policy data\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Listers use in-memory cache from informers\n  - Informers validate etcd connection and watch stream integrity\n  - Authorization falls back to error handling if informer fails\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Requires network-level access; audit trail captures policy changes\n\n#### F. Short-Circuit Logic Abuse in Authorizer Chain\n- **Vector:** Attacker exploits authorizer ordering (e.g., permissive Node authorizer checked first)\n- **Attack Example:** Kubelet-specific request matches Node authorizer before RBAC can deny\n- **Mitigation:**\n  - Authorizer chain order is configuration-dependent\n  - Short-circuit only occurs on Allow/Deny; NoOpinion continues\n  - Each authorizer independent; no state leakage\n- **Risk Level:** MEDIUM \u2014 Depends on chain configuration; documented in authorizer docs\n\n### 2. Vulnerability Classes and Mitigations\n\n#### Authorization Bypass (CWE-285)\n- **Mechanism:** Bypass of policy evaluation through:\n  - Parsing ambiguity (partially mitigated by shared RequestInfo)\n  - Empty authorizer list (code-level check: \"at least one authorization mode\")\n  - Disabled authorization (authorization filter logs warning; bypasses authorization)\n- **Mitigation Strength:** STRONG for parsing; WEAK for disabled authorization\n- **Recommendation:** Enforce authorization mode via startup validation\n\n#### Privilege Escalation (CWE-269)\n- **Mechanism:** User granted excessive permissions through:\n  - Overly permissive roles (no automated validation)\n  - Wildcard selectors in policy rules\n  - Service account privilege inheritance\n- **Mitigation Strength:** WEAK \u2014 Relies on policy discipline\n- **Recommendation:** Implement policy scanning/validation tooling; enforce least-privilege admissions webhooks\n\n#### Information Disclosure (CWE-200)\n- **Mechanism:** Authorization disabled; rules exposed via introspection\n- **Mitigation Strength:** WEAK if authorization disabled\n- **Recommendation:** Mandatory authorization configuration; audit tool to detect disabled authorization\n\n#### Authentication Coercion (CWE-287)\n- **Vector:** Attacker impersonates user by:\n  - Forging request headers (if using header-based auth without mTLS)\n  - Reusing stolen tokens\n- **Mitigation:** Depends on authentication method (certificate validation, token lifecycle)\n- **Risk Level:** HIGH if front-proxy auth without strict validation\n\n### 3. Data Flow Security Properties\n\n#### Immutability of Authorization Input\n- **User Identity:** Once extracted by authentication filter and stored in context, immutable\n- **Request Metadata:** RequestInfo constructed once, shared throughout request lifecycle\n- **Attributes:** AttributesRecord is value-type (passed by copy in Go)\n- **Security Property:** Authorization decisions based on stable, non-modifiable input\n\n#### Stateless Authorization\n- **RBACAuthorizer:** Stateless; no session/cache between requests\n- **DefaultRuleResolver:** Queries fresh authorizer-cached data per request\n- **Security Property:** No cross-request state leakage; replay protection inherent\n\n#### Error Handling\n- **Rule Resolution Errors:** Caught during traversal; cause return of (DecisionNoOpinion, error)\n- **Partial Failures:** If one role lookup fails, other rules still evaluated (partial policy evaluation)\n- **RequestInfo Parse Errors:** InternalError returned; request blocked\n- **Security Property:** Failures generally deny access; graceful degradation possible\n\n### 4. Security Boundaries\n\n#### Authorization Filter Boundary\n- **Input:** HTTP request + context (user, requestInfo)\n- **Output:** Allow/Deny decision\n- **Cross-boundary Trust:** Assumes authentication filter trustworthiness\n\n#### Authorizer Chain Boundary\n- **Union Authorizer:** Orchestrates multiple authorizers\n- **Assumption:** Individual authorizers are trustworthy; no authorization checks between them\n- **Risk:** Single compromised authorizer (e.g., malicious Node authorizer) can permit requests\n\n#### RBAC-to-Storage Boundary\n- **Data Source:** Listers (informer caches) for roles/bindings\n- **Assumption:** Informer cache is synchronized with etcd\n- **Risk:** Stale cache could apply outdated policies (low probability due to watch semantics)\n\n#### User Identity Boundary\n- **Source:** Authentication result (user.Info)\n- **Assumption:** User identity is authentic and complete\n- **Risk:** Authentication compromise propagates to authorization (HIGH severity, out-of-scope for auth)\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Security Controls\n\n### Control 1: RequestInfo Validation\n- **Location:** `authorization.go:100-111`, `requestinfo.go:28-41`\n- **Function:** Ensures request intent is correctly parsed before authorization\n- **Enforcement:** Missing RequestInfo \u2192 InternalError (blocks request)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 RequestInfo construction fails loudly\n\n### Control 2: User Context Injection\n- **Location:** `authentication.go:46-110`\n- **Function:** Authenticates user and injects identity into context\n- **Enforcement:** No authentication \u2192 failed.ServeHTTP (denies request)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 User identity required for authorization\n\n### Control 3: Rule Evaluation\n- **Location:** `rbac.go:75-127`, `rule.go:179-237`\n- **Function:** Enumerates all applicable rules and checks for permission match\n- **Enforcement:** No matching rule \u2192 DecisionNoOpinion (effectively deny)\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Complete rule traversal, no early termination unless rule matches\n\n### Control 4: Subject Matching\n- **Location:** `rule.go:263-300` (`appliesTo`, `appliesToUser`)\n- **Function:** Verifies user matches binding subjects (by name, group, service account)\n- **Enforcement:** appliesToUser() implements strict comparison logic\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Direct string/group comparison; no glob patterns in subject names\n\n### Control 5: Role Reference Resolution\n- **Location:** `rule.go:240-259` (`GetRoleReferenceRules`)\n- **Function:** Validates role reference kind (Role vs. ClusterRole) and looks up rules\n- **Enforcement:** Unknown role reference kind \u2192 error\n- **Bypass Potential:** LOW \u2014 Explicit kind switch, no implicit resolution\n\n---\n\n## Audit and Observability\n\n### Audit Trail\n- **Location:** `authorization.go:80-96`\n- **Information Recorded:**\n  - Decision (allow/forbid)\n  - Reason (e.g., \"RBAC: allowed by ClusterRoleBinding xyz\")\n  - Authorization duration\n- **Audit Events:** Integration with `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit` for request-level logging\n\n### Logging\n- **Decision Denials:** Logged at V=4 level (debug)\n- **Detailed Denials:** Logged at V=5 level (very verbose), showing all attempted rules\n- **Example:** `\"RBAC: no rules authorize user %q with groups %q to %s %s\"`\n\n### Metrics\n- **Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/metrics.go`\n- **Metrics:** Decision counts, latency, error rates by decision type\n\n---\n\n## Known Limitations and Mitigations\n\n| Limitation | Implication | Mitigation |\n|---|---|---|\n| **No Deny Rules** | RBAC is purely additive; cannot explicitly deny | Design policies carefully; use negative space (don't grant permission) |\n| **No Conditional Rules** | Rules cannot depend on runtime context (e.g., time-based) | Use external webhook authorizer for conditional logic |\n| **No Resource Quota/Enforcement** | Authorization doesn't limit resource consumption | Use ResourceQuota and admission webhooks |\n| **Cluster-wide Rules Evaluated for Namespace Requests** | Namespace-scoped requests checked against ClusterRoleBindings | Expected behavior; allows cross-namespace role references |\n| **Service Account Privilege Inheritance** | Service account inherits all bindings in its namespace | Principle of least privilege; separate service accounts per function |\n| **Deprecated Auth Methods** | Legacy ABAC, static files deprecated | Migrate to RBAC or webhook authorization |\n\n---\n\n## Summary: RBAC Authorization Security Posture\n\n### Strengths\n1. **Clear Separation of Concerns:** Authentication (identity) \u2192 Authorization (policy enforcement) \u2192 Admission (resource semantic validation)\n2. **Pluggable Architecture:** Multiple authorizers can coexist; flexible integration with external systems\n3. **Stateless Design:** No cross-request state; immunity to replay/timing attacks\n4. **Default-Deny Model:** Authorizer chain defaults to NoOpinion (deny) if no rule matches\n5. **Audit Integration:** Full request lifecycle logged; decisions and denials traceable\n6. **Informer-based Caching:** Efficient in-memory policy evaluation without etcd query per request\n7. **Short-circuit Semantics:** Both Allow and Deny decisions halt further evaluation; no policy contradiction\n\n### Weaknesses\n1. **Policy Misconfiguration Risk:** No built-in validation of role semantics; overly permissive roles possible\n2. **Service Account Token Compromise:** Once token obtained, full permissions granted without additional checks\n3. **Authorizer Chain Ordering:** Permissive authorizers checked first could permit requests prematurely\n4. **Disabled Authorization:** If authorization mode disabled, all requests allowed (warning only)\n5. **No Time-based or Contextual Rules:** RBAC is static; cannot encode temporal constraints or conditional logic\n\n### Key Security Recommendations\n1. **Enforce Authorization Mode:** Mandate authorization at API server startup (not optional)\n2. **Restrict Service Account Token Scope:** Bind tokens to specific audiences; minimize blast radius if compromised\n3. **Audit Role/Binding Changes:** Monitor for policy modifications; alert on suspicious changes\n4. **Implement Policy Validation:** Scanning tool to detect overly permissive roles before deployment\n5. **Least-Privilege Service Accounts:** Create minimal service accounts for workloads; avoid shared accounts\n6. **Review Authorizer Chain:** Verify ordering; ensure more restrictive authorizers evaluated before permissive ones\n7. **Secure Informer Communication:** Validate informer cache freshness; monitor for sync failures\n8. **Monitor Denial Patterns:** Alert on repeated authorization denials for high-privilege operations\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization system implements a well-architected, defense-in-depth security model. Request authorization is decoupled from authentication and admission, enabling flexible policy enforcement. The stateless, plugin-based design provides strong fundamentals for secure access control. However, the security posture depends critically on proper policy configuration, secure secret management (for service account tokens), and comprehensive audit monitoring. Organizations deploying Kubernetes must combine RBAC with operational discipline (least-privilege design, policy review, incident response) to achieve robust authorization security.\n",

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit

## Executive Summary

The Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem implements a principled, defense-in-depth security model for API request authorization. The flow separates concerns across authentication (identity establishment), request parsing (intent extraction), and authorization decision (rule evaluation). RBAC operates within a pluggable authorizer chain that allows integration with alternative authorization mechanisms (Node, Webhook, ABAC). The implementation demonstrates strong security controls through stateless decision-making, immutable rule definitions, and clear separation of duties.

---

## Files Examined

### Core Authorization Infrastructure
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`** — HTTP filter intercepting requests and invoking authorizer chain; entry point for authorization decisions
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`** — Authorizer interface definitions and AttributesRecord (request metadata carrier)
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** — Authorizer chain composition enabling multiple authorizers with short-circuit allow/deny semantics

### RBAC Authorization Implementation
- **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** — RBACAuthorizer implementation; core rule evaluation and allow/deny decision logic
- **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** — DefaultRuleResolver; role and binding resolution, subject matching, rule accumulation
- **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`** — RBAC authorizer instantiation with informer-based role/binding listers

- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`** — RequestInfo extraction from HT
